      <div class="sqs-slice yui3-widget sqs-slice-heading sqs-slice-heading-content" data-slice-type="heading" data-slice-id="65fa30876f0c382ca70306b5" id="yui_3_17_2_1_1769446668462_245"><h1 id="sqs-slash-page-header" style="display: inline-block;">Land Recognition</h1>
</div>
      <div class="sqs-slice yui3-widget sqs-slice-body sqs-slice-body-content" data-slice-type="body" data-slice-id="65fa30876f0c382ca70306b7" id="yui_3_17_2_1_1769446668462_267"><p class="" style="white-space:pre-wrap;">I acknowledge that my work takes place on unceded Indigenous lands. The Kanien'kha Nation are recognized as the stewards of the land known as Tiohti:ke or Montreal. The Haundenosaunee Confederacy, of which the Kanien'kha Nation is a part, and the Anishinaabeg peoples have strong historical ties to the area. Today, it is home to a diverse population of Indigenous and other peoples. I invite you to take a moment to reflect on whose land you are living and working on, and if you dont know, to research and reflect.</p></div>
